[Jax: Stop returning a list of cost-analyses.](https://github.com/google-research/google-research/commit/72423e8a1f64c74183773f2ed748b646d85b9eb4 "Jax: Stop returning a list of cost-analyses.
As it stands, there is only ever one element in this list (see b/384741132) and only the 0th element is ever used so we can simplify.
This is a potentially breaking change for external users, but (as stated in the [documentation](https://jax.readthedocs.io/en/latest/aot.html#debug-information-and-analyses-when-available)) no guarantees are made on this type, which is intended for debugging purposes and not intended to be a reliable public API.
PiperOrigin-RevId: 715837855")

 | 

[\[Anthea\] Add better support for bidirectional text.](https://github.com/google-research/google-research/commit/8df36a6121df3a4f8243cbf42c53f300e10dad90 "[Anthea] Add better support for bidirectional text.
Bidirectional text is sometimes improperly supported. Specifically, when right-to-left text has embedded left-to-right text at the beginning, the browser assumes that the prevailing order is left-to-right. This change uses the source- and target-language information to infer whether the prevailing direction should be right-to-left.
The list of right-to-left languages and their codes that are supported with this change is:
- Arabic (ar)
- Persian (fa)
- Hebrew (he, iw)
- Urdu (ur)
- Pashto (ps)
- Yiddish (yi)
Note that, with this change, if either the source or target is labeled as a right-to-left language but the text is actually entirely or mostly left-to-right, it will be displayed incorrectly. Users should make sure that language labels are accurate.
PiperOrigin-RevId: 694580275")

The most common source of type errors is that scipy 1.11 changed its sparse matrix class into a base class with only a subset of the properties that it used to have in its type. See https://docs.scipy.org/doc/scipy/release/1.11.0-notes.html#scipy-sparse-improvements and https://docs.scipy.org/doc/scipy/reference/generated/scipy.sparse.spmatrix.html . However, this appears to be a type-only problem since concrete subclasses still have the original properties.

This change migrates users of APIs removed in NumPy 2.0 to their recommended replacements (https://numpy.org/doc/stable/numpy_2_0_migration_guide.html).
This change replaces uses of `np.math`, which is a deprecated alias for the builtin `math` module, with the builtin `math` module. `np.math` is removed in NumPy 2.0.

[Added colab to train linear VAE with analytic or stochastic ELBO comp…](https://github.com/google-research/google-research/commit/c28d8d69cd15ecd059ccee8c7e402d0d9a96c9b3 "Added colab to train linear VAE with analytic or stochastic ELBO computation. Colab includes the following:
- Summary of the linear VAE model and ELBO using markdown
- Linear VAE model which can be trained using either stochastic or analytic ELBO
- Computation of likelihood under pPCA model
- Computation of pPCA MLE solution
- Short training loop for linear VAE, with default settings that achieve near-optimal weights
- Visualization of the training ELBO
- Visualization of the learned weights (verifying orthogonality up to numerical error)

[\[Marot\] Support filtering category names with parentheses.](https://github.com/google-research/google-research/commit/aa119f4f0837a2b3b397dd50aa0e6da86655d5d9 "[Marot] Support filtering category names with parentheses.
Characters that are significant in regular expressions (most notably parentheses) would previously present problems if present in e.g. an error category name: to filter by them, those characters would need to be escaped. This affected both clicking on an element of a result row, and selecting a filter value from the drop-down menus.
Now, special characters are escaped in both cases.
PiperOrigin-RevId: 676078843")

The most common source of type errors is that scipy 1.11 changed its sparse matrix class into a base class with only a subset of the properties that it used to have in its type. See https://docs.scipy.org/doc/scipy/release/1.11.0-notes.html#scipy-sparse-improvements and https://docs.scipy.org/doc/scipy/reference/generated/scipy.sparse.spmatrix.html . However, this appears to be a type-only problem since concrete subclasses still have the original properties.

This change migrates users of APIs removed in NumPy 2.0 to their recommended replacements (https://numpy.org/doc/stable/numpy_2_0_migration_guide.html).
This change replaces uses of `np.math`, which is a deprecated alias for the builtin `math` module, with the builtin `math` module. `np.math` is removed in NumPy 2.0.

This change migrates users of APIs removed in NumPy 2.0 to their recommended replacements (https://numpy.org/doc/stable/numpy_2_0_migration_guide.html).
This CL makes the following changes in colab notebooks:
* np.NaN -> np.nan
* np.NAN -> np.nan
* np.Inf -> np.inf
* np.Infinity -> np.inf
* np.infty -> np.inf
* np.NINF -> -np.inf

[Fix flaky `symbolic/instructions_test.py`.](https://github.com/google-research/google-research/commit/4f4a9bedf5df3fae4de7f3b8da0d2b1475e4641c "Fix flaky `symbolic/instructions_test.py`.
The test was flaky because the `assertAlmostEqual` function from `unittest` module doesn't work correctly with `sympy` floats. Inside the `unittest` module, the difference between values is calculated, rounded and ultimately compared to zero-valued `int`. That comparison always returns `False` for `sympy` float, even when its value is `0.0`.
Due to the above, when at least one of the arguments of `assertAlmostEqual` is `sympy` float, the function raises an exception in case of any difference between the values, ignoring the requested tolerance of 7 decimal places.
The issue seems like a bug in the `sympy` library. As a workaround, we can convert `sympy` float to built-in python float, it solves the issue.
PiperOrigin-RevId: 700735281")

This change migrates users of APIs removed in NumPy 2.0 to their recommended replacements (https://numpy.org/doc/stable/numpy_2_0_migration_guide.html).
This change replaces uses of `np.math`, which is a deprecated alias for the builtin `math` module, with the builtin `math` module. `np.math` is removed in NumPy 2.0.

[\[numpy\] Fix users of NumPy APIs that are removed in NumPy 2.0.](https://github.com/google-research/google-research/commit/3a4e6d63c045e0f77640fd3c31370c38559c6834 "[numpy] Fix users of NumPy APIs that are removed in NumPy 2.0.
This change migrates users of APIs removed in NumPy 2.0 to their recommended replacements (https://numpy.org/doc/stable/numpy_2_0_migration_guide.html).
This change replaces uses of `np.math`, which is a deprecated alias for the builtin `math` module, with the builtin `math` module. `np.math` is removed in NumPy 2.0.

Repository files navigation
---------------------------

*   [README](https://github.com/google-research/google-research?screenshot=true#)
*   [Apache-2.0 license](https://github.com/google-research/google-research?screenshot=true#)

Google Research
===============

[](https://github.com/google-research/google-research?screenshot=true#google-research)

This repository contains code released by [Google Research](https://research.google/).

All datasets in this repository are released under the CC BY 4.0 International license, which can be found here: [https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by/4.0/legalcode](https://creativecommons.org/licenses/by/4.0/legalcode). All source files in this repository are released under the Apache 2.0 license, the text of which can be found in the LICENSE file.

* * *

Because the repo is large, we recommend you download only the subdirectory of interest:

*   Use GitHub editor to open the project. To open the editor change the url from github.com to github.dev in the address bar.
*   In the left navigation panel, right-click on the folder of interest and select download.

If you'd like to submit a pull request, you'll need to clone the repository; we recommend making a shallow clone (without history).

```
git clone git@github.com:google-research/google-research.git --depth=1
```

* * *

_Disclaimer: This is not an official Google product._

Updated in 2023.

\n\n[anthea](https://github.com/google-research/google-research/tree/master/anthea \"anthea\")\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n | \n\n[\\[Anthea\\] Add better support for bidirectional text.](https://github.com/google-research/google-research/commit/8df36a6121df3a4f8243cbf42c53f300e10dad90 \"[Anthea] Add better support for bidirectional text.\nBidirectional text is sometimes improperly supported. Specifically, when right-to-left text has embedded left-to-right text at the beginning, the browser assumes that the prevailing order is left-to-right. This change uses the source- and target-language information to infer whether the prevailing direction should be right-to-left.\nThe list of right-to-left languages and their codes that are supported with this change is:\n- Arabic (ar)\n- Persian (fa)\n- Hebrew (he, iw)\n- Urdu (ur)\n- Pashto (ps)\n- Yiddish (yi)\nNote that, with this change, if either the source or target is labeled as a right-to-left language but the text is actually entirely or mostly left-to-right, it will be displayed incorrectly. Users should make sure that language labels are accurate.\nPiperOrigin-RevId: 694580275\")\n\n\n\n | \n\nNov 8, 2024\n\n |\n| `symbolic/instructions_test.py`.](https://github.com/google-research/google-research/commit/4f4a9bedf5df3fae4de7f3b8da0d2b1475e4641c \"Fix flaky `symbolic/instructions_test.py`.\nThe test was flaky because the `assertAlmostEqual` function from `unittest` module doesn't work correctly with `sympy` floats. Inside the `unittest` module, the difference between values is calculated, rounded and ultimately compared to zero-valued `int`. That comparison always returns `False` for `sympy` float, even when its value is `0.0`.\nDue to the above, when at least one of the arguments of `assertAlmostEqual` is `sympy` float, the function raises an exception in case of any difference between the values, ignoring the requested tolerance of 7 decimal places.\nThe issue seems like a bug in the `sympy` library. As a workaround, we can convert `sympy` float to built-in python float, it solves the issue.\nPiperOrigin-RevId: 700735281\")\n\n\n\n | \n\nNov 27, 2024\n\n |\n|
